We'll have to fix that somehow if\n360: \t * we want to allow parallel inserts in general; updates and deletes have\n361: \t * additional problems especially around combo CIDs.)\n362: \t *\n363: \t * For now, we don't try to use parallel mode if we're running inside a\n364: \t * parallel worker.  We might eventually be able to relax this\n365: \t * restriction, but for now it seems best not to have parallel workers\n366: \t * trying to create their own parallel workers.\n367: \t */\n368: \tif ((cursorOptions & CURSOR_OPT_PARALLEL_OK) != 0 &&\n369: \t\tIsUnderPostmaster &&\n370: \t\tparse->commandType == CMD_SELECT &&\n371: \t\t!parse->hasModifyingCTE &&\n372: \t\tmax_parallel_workers_per_gather > 0 &&\n373: \t\t!IsParallelWorker())\n374: \t{\n375: \t\t/* all the cheap tests pass, so scan the query tree */\n376: \t\tglob->maxParallelHazard = max_parallel_hazard(parse);\n377: \t\tglob->parallelModeOK = (glob->maxParallelHazard != PROPARALLEL_UNSAFE);\n378: \t}\n379: \telse\n380: \t{\n381: \t\t/* skip the query tree scan, just assume it's unsafe */\n382: \t\tglob->maxParallelHazard = PROPARALLEL_UNSAFE;\n383: \t\tglob->parallelModeOK = false;\n384: \t}\n385: \n386: \t/*\n387: \t * glob->parallelModeNeeded is normally set to false here and changed to\n388: \t * true during plan creation if a Gather or Gather Merge plan is actually\n389: \t * created (cf. create_gather_plan, create_gather_merge_plan).\n390: \t *\n391: \t * However, if debug_parallel_query = on or debug_parallel_query =\n392: \t * regress, then we impose parallel mode whenever it's safe to do so, even\n393: \t * if the final plan doesn't use parallelism.  It's not safe to do so if\n394: \t * the query contains anything parallel-unsafe; parallelModeOK will be\n395: \t * false in that case. Use a GUC parameter to decide\n414: \t\t * what fraction to optimize for.\n415: \t\t */\n416: \t\ttuple_fraction = cursor_tuple_fraction;\n417: \n418: \t\t/*\n419: \t\t * We document cursor_tuple_fraction as simply being a fraction, which\n420: \t\t * means the edge cases 0 and 1 have to be treated specially here. The plan tree is essentially\\n7: a demand-pull pipeline of tuple processing operations.  Each node, when\\n8: called, will produce the next tuple in its output sequence, or NULL if no\\n9: more tuples are available.  If the node is not a primitive relation-scanning\\n10: node, it will have child node(s) that it calls in turn to obtain input\\n11: tuples.\\n12: \\n13: Refinements on this basic model include:\\n14: \\n15: * Choice of scan direction (forwards or backwards).  Caution: this is not\\n16: currently well-supported.  It works for primitive scan nodes, but not very\\n17: well for joins, aggregates, etc.\\n18: \\n19: * Rescan command to reset a node and make it generate its output sequence\\n20: over again.\\n21: \\n22: * Parameters that can alter a node's results.  After adjusting a parameter,\\n23: the rescan command must be applied to that node and all nodes above it.\\n24: There is a moderately intelligent scheme to avoid rescanning nodes\\n25: unnecessarily (for example, Sort does not rescan its input if no parameters\\n26: of the input have changed, since it can just reread its stored sorted data).\\n27: \\n28: For a SELECT, it is only necessary to deliver the top-level result tuples\\n29: to the client.  For INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE/MERGE, the actual table modification\\n30: operations happen in a top-level ModifyTable plan node.  If the query\\n31: includes a RETURNING clause, the ModifyTable node delivers the computed\\n32: RETURNING rows as output, otherwise it returns nothing.  Handling INSERT\\n33: is pretty straightforward: the tuples returned from the plan tree below\\n34: ModifyTable are inserted into the correct result relation.  For UPDATE,\\n35: the plan tree returns the new values of the updated columns, plus \\\"junk\\\"\\n36: (hidden) column(s) identifying which table row is to be updated.  The\\n37: ModifyTable node must fetch that row to extract values for the unchanged\\n38: columns, combine the values into a new row, and apply the update.  (For a\\n39: heap table, the row-identity junk column is a CTID, but other things may\\n40: be used for other table types.)  For DELETE, the plan tree need only deliver\\n41: junk row-identity column(s), and the ModifyTable node visits each of those\\n42: rows and marks the row deleted.  MERGE is described below.\\n43: \\n44: XXX a great deal more documentation needs to be written here...\\n45: \\n46: \\n47: Plan Trees and State Trees\\n48: --------------------------\\n49: \\n50: The plan tree delivered by the planner contains a tree of Plan nodes (struct\\n51: types derived from struct Plan).  During executor startup we build a parallel\\n52: tree of identical structure containing executor state nodes --- generally,\\n53: every plan node type has a corresponding executor state node type.  Each node\\n54: in the state tree has a pointer to its corresponding node in the plan tree,\\n55: plus executor state data as needed to implement that node type.  This\\n56: arrangement allows the plan tree to be completely read-only so far as the\\n57: executor is concerned: all data that is modified during execution is in the\\n58: state tree.  Read-only plan trees make life much simpler for plan caching and\\n59: reuse.\\n60: \\n61: A corresponding executor state node may not be created during executor startup\\n62: if the executor determines that an entire subplan is not required due to\\n63: execution time partition pruning determining that no matching records will be\\n64: found there.  This currently only occurs for Append and MergeAppend nodes.  In\\n65: this case the non-required subplans are ignored and the executor state's\\n66: subnode array will become out of sequence to the plan's subplan list.\\n67: \\n68: Each Plan node may have expression trees associated with it, to represent\\n69: its target list, qualification conditions, etc.  These trees are also\\n70: read-only to the executor, but the executor state for expression evaluation\\n71: does not mirror the Plan expression's tree shape, as explained below.\\n72: Rather, there's just one ExprState node per expression tree, although this\\n73: may have sub-nodes for some complex expression node types.\\n74: \\n75: Altogether there are four classes of nodes used in these trees: Plan nodes,\\n76: their corresponding PlanState nodes, Expr nodes, and ExprState nodes.\\n77: (Actually, there are also List nodes, which are used as \\\"glue\\\" in all\\n78: three tree-based representations.)\\n79: \\n80: \\n81: Expression Trees and ExprState nodes\\n82: ------------------------------------\\n83: \\n84: Expression trees, in contrast to Plan trees, are not mirrored into a\\n85: corresponding tree of state nodes.  Instead each separately executable\\n86: expression tree (e.g. a Plan's qual or targetlist) is represented by one\\n87: ExprState node.  The ExprState node contains the information needed to\\n88: evaluate the expression in a compact, linear form.  That compact form is\\n89: stored as a flat array in ExprState->steps[] (an array of ExprEvalStep,\\n90: not ExprEvalStep *).\\n91: \\n92: The reasons for choosing such a representation include:\\n93: - commonly the amount of work needed to evaluate one Expr-type node is\\n94:   small enough that the overhead of having to perform a tree-walk\\n95:   during evaluation is significant.\\n96: - the flat representation can be evaluated non-recursively within a single\\n97:   function, reducing stack depth and function call overhead.\\n98: - such a representation is usable both for fast interpreted execution,\\n99:   and for compiling into native code.\\n100: \\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/postgres--5a461dc4@eb8f07549ee15f0db57589c5f333de3f874fe855/-/blob/src/backend/executor/README%3FL1-100\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"cbfe0f56-e885-4639-b70b-99245de36ee5","uuid":"b5e79290-d6ce-4f57-8362-cbbe3e5678c5","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: src/backend/executor/README\\n2: \\n3: The Postgres Executor\\n4: =====================\\n5: \\n6: The executor processes a tree of \\\"plan nodes\\\". For DELETE, the plan tree need only deliver\n41: junk row-identity column(s), and the ModifyTable node visits each of those\n42: rows and marks the row deleted.  MERGE is described below.\n43: \n44: XXX a great deal more documentation needs to be written here...\n45: \n46: \n47: Plan Trees and State Trees\n48: --------------------------\n49: \n50: The plan tree delivered by the planner contains a tree of Plan nodes (struct\n51: types derived from struct Plan).  During executor startup we build a parallel\n52: tree of identical structure containing executor state nodes --- generally,\n53: every plan node type has a corresponding executor state node type.  Each node\n54: in the state tree has a pointer to its corresponding node in the plan tree,\n55: plus executor state data as needed to implement that node type.  This\n56: arrangement allows the plan tree to be completely read-only so far as the\n57: executor is concerned: all data that is modified during execution is in the\n58: state tree.  Read-only plan trees make life much simpler for plan caching and\n59: reuse.\n60: \n61: A corresponding executor state node may not be created during executor startup\n62: if the executor determines that an entire subplan is not required due to\n63: execution time partition pruning determining that no matching records will be\n64: found there.  This currently only occurs for Append and MergeAppend nodes.  In\n65: this case the non-required subplans are ignored and the executor state's\n66: subnode array will become out of sequence to the plan's subplan list.\n67: \n68: Each Plan node may have expression trees associated with it, to represent\n69: its target list, qualification conditions, etc.  These trees are also\n70: read-only to the executor, but the executor state for expression evaluation\n71: does not mirror the Plan expression's tree shape, as explained below.\n72: Rather, there's just one ExprState node per expression tree, although this\n73: may have sub-nodes for some complex expression node types.\n74: \n75: Altogether there are four classes of nodes used in these trees: Plan nodes,\n76: their corresponding PlanState nodes, Expr nodes, and ExprState nodes.\n77: (Actually, there are also List nodes, which are used as \"glue\" in all\n78: three tree-based representations.)\n79: \n80: \n81: Expression Trees and ExprState nodes\n82: ------------------------------------\n83: \n84: Expression trees, in contrast to Plan trees, are not mirrored into a\n85: corresponding tree of state nodes.  Instead each separately executable\n86: expression tree (e.g. a Plan's qual or targetlist) is represented by one\n87: ExprState node.  The ExprState node contains the information needed to\n88: evaluate the expression in a compact, linear form.  That compact form is\n89: stored as a flat array in ExprState->steps[] (an array of ExprEvalStep,\n90: not ExprEvalStep *).\n91: \n92: The reasons for choosing such a representation include:\n93: - commonly the amount of work needed to evaluate one Expr-type node is\n94:   small enough that the overhead of having to perform a tree-walk\n95:   during evaluation is significant.\n96: - the flat representation can be evaluated non-recursively within a single\n97:   function, reducing stack depth and function call overhead.\n98: - such a representation is usable both for fast interpreted execution,\n99:   and for compiling into native code.\n100: \n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/postgres--5a461dc4@eb8f07549ee15f0db57589c5f333de3f874fe855/-/blob/src/backend/executor/README%3FL1-100"}}}

— Initialize trigger handling\n\nVOLCANO-STYLE EXECUTION:\n├─ ExecutorRun(QueryDesc, ForwardScanDirection, 0) [src/backend/executor/execMain.c:297]\n│   ├─ ExecutePlan(estate, estate->planstate, VOLCANO-STYLE DISPATCH (demand-pull pipeline):\n│   │       │   ├─ if node is SeqScanState:\n│   │       │   │   └─ ExecSeqScan() → Returns next tuple\n│   │       │   ├─ else if node is each left tuple, calls ExecProcNode(right_planstate)\n│   │       │   │   ├─ Evaluates join condition\n│   │       │   │   └─ Returns joined tuple if condition passes\n│   │       │   ├─ else if node is HashJoinState:\n│   │       │   │   └─ ExecHashJoin() — Hash-based join\n│   │       │   ├─ else if node is AggState:\n│   │       │   │   └─ ExecAgg() — Aggregate computation\n│   │       │   └─ ... other node types\n│   │       ├─ ExecEvalExpr() [src/backend/executor/execExpr.c]\n│   │       │   └─ Evaluate expressions in per-tuple context\n│   │       ├─ ResetExprContext() — Clear per-tuple memory\n│   │       └─ Return TupleTableSlot\n│   ├─ Send tuple to dest receiver (result display, INSERT INTO, etc.)\n│   └─ Repeat until no more tuples or count exhausted\n\nEXECUTOR FINALIZATION:\n├─ ExecutorFinish(QueryDesc) [src/backend/executor/execMain.c]\n│   └─ ExecPostprocessPlan() — Finish any unfinished ModifyTable nodes\n└─ ExecutorEnd(QueryDesc) [src/backend/executor/execMain.c:466]\n    ├─ ExecEndNode() [src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c:215]\n    │   ├─ Recursively finalizes entire PlanState tree\n    │   ├─ Close table/index scans\n    │   ├─ Release buffer pins\n    │   ├─ Free hash tables, sort buffers, etc.\n    │   └─ ExecEndSeqScan(), ExecEndNestLoop(), ExecEndAgg(), ...\n    ├─ AfterTriggerEndQuery() — Finalize triggers\n    └─ FreeExecutorState() — Free per-query context\n```\n\n**Volcano-Style Executor Dispatch:**\n- Each PlanState node has a slot function pointer (`ps_ProcNode`)\n- ExecProcNode() calls the node's function\n- Each node implementation:\n  1. Calls ExecProcNode() on child nodes (demand-pull)\n  2. Evaluates filters/aggregations\n  3. Returns next tuple or NULL\n- Execution is recursive top-down data flow bottom-up\n- Each node executes until it exhausts its input\n- Memory is freed in a per-tuple context to avoid accumulation\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n#### 1. **Pipeline Architecture (Data Flow Pattern)**\nThe query execution follows a classic staged pipeline where each stage transforms the input into a higher-level representation:\n- **Lexical** (raw text) → **Syntactic** (RawStmt) → **Semantic** (Query) → **Logical** (Query after rewrite) → **Physical** (PlannedStmt) → **Execution** (PlanState)\n\nEach stage is independent and operates on well-defined data structures that are passed to the next stage.\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Optimization (Optimizer Pattern)**\nThe planner uses a two-phase optimization strategy:\n1. **Path Phase**: Generates multiple Path alternatives with cost estimates, explores join orderings, index availability\n2. **Plan Phase**: Converts the best Path to an executable Plan tree\n\nThis separation allows the optimizer to explore many paths efficiently without generating full Plan trees for each alternative.\n\n#### 3. **Volcano Model Executor (Iterator Pattern)**\nThe executor implements the Volcano/Cascades iterator model:\n- Each PlanState node is a module that produces one tuple at a time\n- When called, a node:\n  1. Calls its children to get tuples (demand-pull)\n  2. Applies its operation (scan, join, aggregate, etc.)\n  3. Returns the result tuple\n- This is implemented via function pointers in PlanState nodes\n- Allows for:\n  - Pipelined execution (no need to materialize all intermediate results)\n  - Partial/LIMIT execution (stop when limit is reached)\n  - Streaming joins and aggregations\n\n#### 4. **Parallel Read-Only Data Structures (Plan Tree)**\n- **Plan Tree** (created by planner) is read-only throughout execution\n- **PlanState Tree** (created by executor) is the mutable execution state\n- This separation allows plan reuse without modification\n\n#### 5. **Context-Based Memory Management**\n- Per-query context: Holds query plan and long-lived data\n- Per-tuple context: Holds temporary per-tuple expression evaluation results\n- Contexts are freed hierarchically to avoid memory leaks\n\n#### 6. **Hook-Based Extensibility**\nPostgreSQL allows plugins to intercept execution at multiple points:\n- `planner_hook` - Plugin planner implementation\n- `ExecutorStart_hook`, `ExecutorRun_hook`, `ExecutorEnd_hook` - Plugin executor hooks\n- `post_parse_analyze_hook` - Post-analysis hook\n- This enables extensions, query logging, and custom planning strategies\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility | Data Structures |\n|-----------|-----------------|-----------------|\n| **Traffic Cop (exec_simple_query)** | Orchestrate pipeline, manage contexts, transaction control | RawStmt list → Query list → PlannedStmt list |\n| **Lexer (scan.l)** | Tokenize SQL string | Raw characters → Token stream |\n| **Parser (gram.y)** | Build parse tree from tokens | Token stream → RawStmt (SelectStmt/InsertStmt/etc.) |\n| **Analyzer** | Semantic validation, resolve references | RawStmt → Query (with rtable, joins validated) |\n| **Rewriter** | Apply rules, views, RLS policies | Query → Query list (possibly expanded) |\n| **Planner/Path Generator** | Generate alternative execution paths | Query → RelOptInfo with Path list (Paths with costs) |\n| **Planner/Plan Creator** | Convert best path to executable plan | Best Path → Plan tree (SeqScan/NestLoop/etc.) |\n| **Executor** | Execute plan tree | PlannedStmt + PlanState tree → Result tuples |\n| **Portal** | Interface between protocol and executor | Holds PlannedStmt and manages snapshots/resources |\n\n### Data Flow Through Pipeline\n\n```\nRaw SQL String\n    ↓ [LEXER: scan.l]\nToken Stream\n    ↓ [PARSER: gram.y]\nRawStmt (SelectStmt/InsertStmt/UpdateStmt/etc.)\n    ↓ [ANALYZER: analyze.c + parse_*.c]\nQuery (analyzed, resolved references)\n    ↓ [REWRITER: rewriteHandler.c]\nQuery (after rules, views, RLS applied)\n    ↓ [OPTIMIZER PATH PHASE: allpaths.c, costsize.c]\nRelOptInfo trees with Path lists (alternatives with costs)\n    ↓ [OPTIMIZER SELECT BEST PATH]\nCheapest Path tree\n    ↓ [OPTIMIZER PLAN PHASE: createplan.c]\nPlannedStmt (Plan tree: SeqScan/NestLoop/etc.)\n    ↓ [PORTAL SETUP]\nQueryDesc (PlannedStmt + metadata)\n    ↓ [EXECUTOR INIT: ExecInitNode]\nPlanState tree (parallel structure to Plan tree)\n    ↓ [EXECUTOR RUN: ExecProcNode via Volcano dispatch]\nTupleTableSlot (results sent to dest receiver)\n    ↓ [EXECUTOR END: ExecEndNode cleanup]\nQuery Completion\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n1. **Parser → Analyzer**: RawStmt must have valid stmt node (SelectStmt, InsertStmt, etc.). Analyzer produces Query with all references resolved.\n\n2. **Analyzer → Rewriter**: Query is complete and analyzable. Rewriter may produce multiple Queries (view expansion) or modified single Query.\n\n3. **Rewriter → Optimizer**: Query is fully analyzed and rewritten. Optimizer produces PlannedStmt with complete Plan tree.\n\n4. **Optimizer → Executor**: PlannedStmt.planTree must be valid Plan node tree with all necessary metadata (cost, cardinality estimates). Executor produces PlanState mirror tree.\n\n5. **Executor → Destination**: Each call to ExecProcNode() returns a TupleTableSlot (or NULL when done). Dest receiver processes each tuple.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe PostgreSQL query execution pipeline implements a classical database architecture with careful separation of concerns. Starting from the raw SQL string in `exec_simple_query()`, the query flows through:\n\n1. **Parser** (Flex/Bison) produces abstract syntax trees\n2. **Semantic Analyzer** validates and resolves all references against the catalog\n3. **Rewriter** applies database rules, views, and row-level security policies\n4. **Two-Phase Optimizer** explores alternative execution paths and selects the best one\n5. **Volcano-Style Executor** executes the plan tree using a demand-pull pipeline model\n\nEach stage operates on progressively more refined data structures (RawStmt → Query → PlannedStmt → PlanState), enabling plan caching, parallelization, and plugin extensibility. The Volcano executor's iterator model allows PostgreSQL to efficiently handle large result sets through pipelined execution and memory-efficient per-tuple processing.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":153,"cache_read_input_tokens":89600,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":153},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"cbfe0f56-e885-4639-b70b-99245de36ee5","uuid":"dfd419e0-ccb0-4b70-8f85-1d50a2b18a80"}

function\n- Each node implementation:\n  1. Calls ExecProcNode() on child nodes (demand-pull)\n  2. Evaluates filters/aggregations\n  3. Returns next tuple or NULL\n- Execution is recursive top-down data flow bottom-up\n- Each node executes until it exhausts its input\n- Memory is freed in a per-tuple context to avoid accumulation\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n#### 1. **Pipeline Architecture (Data Flow Pattern)**\nThe query execution follows a classic staged pipeline where each stage transforms the input into a higher-level representation:\n- **Lexical** (raw text) → **Syntactic** (RawStmt) → **Semantic** (Query) → **Logical** (Query after rewrite) → **Physical** (PlannedStmt) → **Execution** (PlanState)\n\nEach stage is independent and operates on well-defined data structures that are passed to the next stage.\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Optimization (Optimizer Pattern)**\nThe planner uses a two-phase optimization strategy:\n1. **Path Phase**: Generates multiple Path alternatives with cost estimates, explores join orderings, index availability\n2. **Plan Phase**: Converts the best Path to an executable Plan tree\n\nThis separation allows the optimizer to explore many paths efficiently without generating full Plan trees for each alternative.\n\n#### 3. **Volcano Model Executor (Iterator Pattern)**\nThe executor implements the Volcano/Cascades iterator model:\n- Each PlanState node is a module that produces one tuple at a time\n- When called, a node:\n  1. Calls its children to get tuples (demand-pull)\n  2. Applies its operation (scan, join, aggregate, etc.)\n  3. Returns the result tuple\n- This is implemented via function pointers in PlanState nodes\n- Allows for:\n  - Pipelined execution (no need to materialize all intermediate results)\n  - Partial/LIMIT execution (stop when limit is reached)\n  - Streaming joins and aggregations\n\n#### 4. **Parallel Read-Only Data Structures (Plan Tree)**\n- **Plan Tree** (created by planner) is read-only throughout execution\n- **PlanState Tree** (created by executor) is the mutable execution state\n- This separation allows plan reuse without modification\n\n#### 5. **Context-Based Memory Management**\n- Per-query context: Holds query plan and long-lived data\n- Per-tuple context: Holds temporary per-tuple expression evaluation results\n- Contexts are freed hierarchically to avoid memory leaks\n\n#### 6. **Hook-Based Extensibility**\nPostgreSQL allows plugins to intercept execution at multiple points:\n- `planner_hook` - Plugin planner implementation\n- `ExecutorStart_hook`, `ExecutorRun_hook`, `ExecutorEnd_hook` - Plugin executor hooks\n- `post_parse_analyze_hook` - Post-analysis hook\n- This enables extensions, query logging, and custom planning strategies\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility | Data Structures |\n|-----------|-----------------|-----------------|\n| **Traffic Cop (exec_simple_query)** | Orchestrate pipeline, manage contexts, transaction control | RawStmt list → Query list → PlannedStmt list |\n| **Lexer (scan.l)** | Tokenize SQL string | Raw characters → Token stream |\n| **Parser (gram.y)** | Build parse tree from tokens | Token stream → RawStmt (SelectStmt/InsertStmt/etc.) |\n| **Analyzer** | Semantic validation, resolve references | RawStmt → Query (with rtable, joins validated) |\n| **Rewriter** | Apply rules, views, RLS policies | Query → Query list (possibly expanded) |\n| **Planner/Path Generator** | Generate alternative execution paths | Query → RelOptInfo with Path list (Paths with costs) |\n| **Planner/Plan Creator** | Convert best path to executable plan | Best Path → Plan tree (SeqScan/NestLoop/etc.) |\n| **Executor** | Execute plan tree | PlannedStmt + PlanState tree → Result tuples |\n| **Portal** | Interface between protocol and executor | Holds PlannedStmt and manages snapshots/resources |\n\n### Data Flow Through Pipeline\n\n```\nRaw SQL String\n    ↓ [LEXER: scan.l]\nToken Stream\n    ↓ [PARSER: gram.y]\nRawStmt (SelectStmt/InsertStmt/UpdateStmt/etc.)\n    ↓ [ANALYZER: analyze.c + parse_*.c]\nQuery (analyzed, resolved references)\n    ↓ [REWRITER: rewriteHandler.c]\nQuery (after rules, views, RLS applied)\n    ↓ [OPTIMIZER PATH PHASE: allpaths.c, costsize.c]\nRelOptInfo trees with Path lists (alternatives with costs)\n    ↓ [OPTIMIZER SELECT BEST PATH]\nCheapest Path tree\n    ↓ [OPTIMIZER PLAN PHASE: createplan.c]\nPlannedStmt (Plan tree: SeqScan/NestLoop/etc.)\n    ↓ [PORTAL SETUP]\nQueryDesc (PlannedStmt + metadata)\n    ↓ [EXECUTOR INIT: ExecInitNode]\nPlanState tree (parallel structure to Plan tree)\n    ↓ [EXECUTOR RUN: ExecProcNode via Volcano dispatch]\nTupleTableSlot (results sent to dest receiver)\n    ↓ [EXECUTOR END: ExecEndNode cleanup]\nQuery Completion\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n1. **Parser → Analyzer**: RawStmt must have valid stmt node (SelectStmt, InsertStmt, etc.). Analyzer produces Query with all references resolved.\n\n2. **Analyzer → Rewriter**: Query is complete and analyzable. Rewriter may produce multiple Queries (view expansion) or modified single Query.\n\n3. **Rewriter → Optimizer**: Query is fully analyzed and rewritten. Optimizer produces PlannedStmt with complete Plan tree.\n\n4. **Optimizer → Executor**: PlannedStmt.planTree must be valid Plan node tree with all necessary metadata (cost, cardinality estimates). Executor produces PlanState mirror tree.\n\n5. **Executor → Destination**: Each call to ExecProcNode() returns a TupleTableSlot (or NULL when done). Dest receiver processes each tuple.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe PostgreSQL query execution pipeline implements a classical database architecture with careful separation of concerns. Starting from the raw SQL string in `exec_simple_query()`, the query flows through:\n\n1. **Parser** (Flex/Bison) produces abstract syntax trees\n2. **Semantic Analyzer** validates and resolves all references against the catalog\n3. **Rewriter** applies database rules, views, and row-level security policies\n4. **Two-Phase Optimizer** explores alternative execution paths and selects the best one\n5. **Volcano-Style Executor** executes the plan tree using a demand-pull pipeline model\n\nEach stage operates on progressively more refined data structures (RawStmt → Query → PlannedStmt → PlanState), enabling plan caching, parallelization, and plugin extensibility. The Volcano executor's iterator model allows PostgreSQL to efficiently handle large result sets through pipelined execution and memory-efficient per-tuple processing.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
